### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 1 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company that makes wildlife videos purchases camera equipment for $\$ 32,400$. The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, after which it is considered to have no monetary value. How much is the camera equipment worth 4 years after it is purchased?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 10,800$
  B: $\$ 16,200$
  C: $\$ 21,600$
  D: $\$ 29,700$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment has no monetary value.
  Therefore, the equipment depreciates $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700$ per year.
  4 years after the equipment is purchased, the equipment has depreciated $\$ 2,700 \cdot 4 = \$ 10,800$.
  The value of the equipment after 4 years is $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years.
  The depreciation rate per year is $r=\frac{\$ 32,400}{12\text{ years}}=\$ 2,700$.
  After 4 years, the equipment will have depreciated by $4r=\$ 10,800$.
  The current value of the equipment is $V=\$ 32,400 - 4r = \$ 21,600$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $\$ 21,600$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment has no monetary value.
  The depreciation rate is $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700/\text{year}$.
  After 4 years, the equipment has depreciated $\$ 2,700/\text{year} \times 4 \text{ years} = \$ 10,800$ in value.
  Therefore, the equipment is worth $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$ after 4 years.
Action: Answer("C")

Thought:

  After 12 years, it has no monetary value.

  4 years after the purchase, the equipment would have depreciated by $4 \times 2700 = 10800$ dollars.
  The value of the equipment after 4 years is $32400 - 10800 = 21600$ dollars.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 4:
Thought:

Action: Answer("C")
Response 5:
Thought:
  The camera equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  Therefore, the equipment depreciates linearly over 12 years.
  Let's find the rate of depreciation per year.
  The initial value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400$.
  After 12 years, the value of the equipment is $\$ 0$.
  Let's use the slope-intercept form of a linear equation: $y = mx + b$, where $y$ is the value of the equipment, $x$ is the number of years after purchase, $m$ is the rate of depreciation per year, and $b$ is the initial value of the equipment.
  We can use the two points $(0, 32400)$ and $(12, 0)$ to find the equation of the line:
  $m = \frac{0 - 32400}{12 - 0} = -2700$
  The equation of the line is: $y = -2700x + 32400$
  To find the value of the equipment 4 years after it is purchased, we can plug in $x=4$ into the equation:
  $y = -2700(4) + 32400 = 21600$
  Therefore, the camera equipment is worth $\$ 21,600$ 4 years after it is purchased.

  Therefore, the equipment depreciates linearly over 12 years.
  The depreciation rate per year is the same.
  Let the initial value of the equipment be $V_0 = \$ 32,400$.
  After 12 years, the value of the equipment is 0.
  Let the value of the equipment after 4 years be $V_4$.
  Then, the depreciation rate per year is $\frac{V_0 - 0}{12} = \$ 2,700$.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 9:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years, which means the depreciation per year is constant.
  Let's call the depreciation rate per year "d".
  After 12 years, the equipment has no monetary value, which means the initial value of the equipment is equal to the accumulated depreciation over 12 years.
  Let's call the initial value of the equipment "V".
  After 4 years, the equipment has depreciated by 4d, so its value is V - 4d.
  We need to find V - 4d.
  Since V = 32,400 and it depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years, we have:
  V - 12d = 0
  Solving for V, we get:
  V = 12d
  Substituting V = 12d into V - 4d, we get:
  V - 4d = 8d
  Therefore, we need to find 8d.
  Since V - 12d = 0, we have:
  d = V/12 = 32,400/12 = 2,700
  Substituting d = 2,700 into 8d, we get:
  8d = 8 * 2,700 = 21,600
  Therefore, the camera equipment is worth $\$ 21,600$ 4 years after it is purchased.

Question: $$\frac{a-b}{a}=c$$In the equation above, if $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: $c>1$
  B: $c=1$
  C: $c=-1$
  D: $c<-1$

Thought:

  Since $a$ is negative, $|a|=-a$ and $a<0$.
  Therefore, $\frac{a-b}{a}>1$.
  So, $c>1$.

  Therefore, $h(5)-h(3)=24$.

Question: If $f(x)=\frac{x^{2}-6 x+3}{x-1}$, what is $f(-1)$ ?
Choices:
  A: -5
  B: -2
  C: 2
  D: 5
Response 0:
Thought:
  $f(x)=\frac{x^{2}-6 x+3}{x-1}$ can be simplified using polynomial division or factoring.
  Factoring, we get $f(x)=\frac{(x-3)(x-1)}{x-1} = x-3$.
  Therefore, $f(-1)=-1-3=-4$.
Action: Answer("None of the Above") - The answer is not one of the available choices. The correct answer is -4.
Response 1:
Thought:
  $f(x)=\frac{x^{2}-6 x+3}{x-1}$ is a rational function.
  To find $f(-1)$, we need to substitute $-1$ for $x$ in the function and simplify.
  $f(-1)=\frac{(-1)^{2}-6(-1)+3}{-1-1}$
  $f(-1)=\frac{1+6+3}{-2}$
  $f(-1)=\frac{10}{-2}$
  $f(-1)=-5$
  Therefore, the answer is A: -5.

Topic: Math
Question: A cylindrical can containing pieces of fruit is filled to the top with syrup before being sealed. The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, and the height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$. If $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ of syrup is needed to fill the can to the top, which of the following is closest to the total volume of the pieces of fruit in the can?
Choices:
  A: $7.5 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  B: $185 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The volume of the syrup is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The formula for the volume of a cylinder is $V = \pi r^{2}h$.
  We know the area of the base of the cylinder is $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$.
  We can find the radius of the cylinder by using the formula for the area of a circle: $A = \pi r^{2}$.
  Solving for $r$, we get $r = \sqrt{\frac{75}{\pi}} \approx 4.33 \mathrm{~cm}$.
  Therefore, the volume of the cylinder is $V = \pi (4.33)^{2}(10) \approx 591.46 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The volume of the fruit is the difference between the volume of the cylinder and the volume of the syrup: $V_{fruit} = 591.46 - 110 \approx 481.46 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The closest answer choice to $481.46 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ is D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The can is filled with syrup to the top, so the volume of the syrup is equal to the volume of the can.
  The volume of the can is the product of the area of the base and the height of the can.
  The volume of the can is $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2} \times 10 \mathrm{~cm} = 750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The volume of the fruit is the difference between the total volume of the can and the volume of the syrup.
  The volume of the fruit is $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} = 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.

  The can is cylindrical, so its volume is $V_{\text{cyl}} = \pi r^{2} h$, where $r$ is the radius of the base and $h$ is the height of the can.
  The volume of syrup needed to fill the can is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  Therefore, $V_{\text{cyl}} = 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, so $r^{2} \pi = 75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$.
  Therefore, $r = \sqrt{75/\pi} \approx 4.33 \mathrm{~cm}$.
  The volume of the fruit in the can is equal to $V_{\text{cyl}}$ minus the volume of the syrup.
  The volume of the syrup is equal to the area of the base times the height of the syrup, so $V_{\text{syrup}} = 75h$.
  Therefore, the volume of the fruit is $V_{\text{fruit}} = V_{\text{cyl}} - V_{\text{syrup}} = \pi r^{2} h - 75h$.
  Plugging in the values for $r$ and $h$, we get $V_{\text{fruit}} \approx 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The closest answer choice is C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 9:
Thought:
  The volume of the syrup needed to fill the can is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$, which is also the height of the fruit in the can.
  The formula for the volume of a cylinder is $V = Bh$, where $B$ is the base area and $h$ is the height of the cylinder.
  Therefore, the volume of the can is $V_{can} = Bh = 75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2} \cdot 10 \mathrm{~cm} = 750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The volume of the fruit in the can is the difference between the volume of the can and the volume of the syrup, which is $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} = 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The answer is C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 8 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{array}{r}3 x+4 y=-23 \\2 y-x=-19\end{array}$$What is the solution $(x, y)$ to the system of equations above?
Choices:
  A: $(-5,-2)$
  B: $(3,-8)$
  C: $(4,-6)$
  D: $(9,-6)$
Response 0:
Thought: 
We can solve the system of equations using substitution or elimination method. Let's use the elimination method:
- Multiply the second equation by 3 and add it to the first equation to eliminate x: 
    $$\begin{array}{r}3 x+4 y=-23 \\-x+6 y=-57\end{array}$$
- Add the two equations together to solve for y:
    $$10y=-80 \Rightarrow y=-8$$
- Substitute y=-8 into one of the equations to solve for x:
    $$2(-8)-x=-19 \Rightarrow x=3$$
- Therefore, the solution to the system of equations is (x,y) = (3,-8)
- The answer is B: $(3,-8)$
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We can solve for $x$ in the second equation and substitute it into the first equation to solve for $y$.
  $$2y-x=-19$$
  $$2y= x-19$$
  $$y = \frac{1}{2}x - \frac{19}{2}$$
  Substituting into the first equation:
  $$3x + 4(\frac{1}{2}x - \frac{19}{2}) = -23$$
  $$3x + 2x - 38 = -23$$
  $$5x = 15$$
  $$x = 3$$
  Substituting $x=3$ into $y = \frac{1}{2}x - \frac{19}{2}$:
  $$y = \frac{1}{2}(3) - \frac{19}{2}$$
  $$y = -8$$
  Therefore, the solution is $(x,y) = (3,-8)$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  We can solve this system of equations using elimination or substitution method.
  Let's use substitution method.
  Rearranging the second equation, we get $x=2y+19$.
  Substituting this value of $x$ in the first equation, we get $3(2y+19)+4y=-23$.
  Simplifying this expression, we get $10y=-80$, so $y=-8$.
  Substituting this value of $y$ back into the second equation, we get $x=2(-8)+19=3$.
  Therefore, the solution is $(x,y)=(3,-8)$.
  The answer is B: $(3,-8)$.

Context: $$.a=1,052+1.08 t.$$.The speed of a sound wave in air depends on the air temperature. The formula above shows the relationship between $a$, the speed of a sound wave, in feet per second, and $t$, the air temperature, in degrees Fahrenheit $\left({ }^{\circ} \mathrm{F}\right)$.
Question: Which of the following expresses the air temperature in terms of the speed of a sound wave?
Choices:
  A: $t=\frac{a-1,052}{1.08}$
  B: $t=\frac{a+1,052}{1.08}$
  C: $t=\frac{1,052-a}{1.08}$
  D: $t=\frac{1.08}{a+1,052}$

  Subtracting $1,052$ from both sides gives $a-1,052=1.08t$.
  Dividing both sides by $1.08$ gives $\frac{a-1,052}{1.08}=t$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $t=\frac{a-1,052}{1.08}$.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 10 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $2 w+4 t=14$ and $4 w+5 t=25$, what is the value of $2 w+3 t ?$
Choices:
  A: 6
  B: 10
  C: 13
  D: 17
Response 0:
Thought:
  We are given two equations:
  $2 w+4 t=14\quad \Rightarrow\quad w+2t=7$
  $4 w+5 t=25\quad \Rightarrow\quad 4w+5t=25$
  We need to find the value of $2 w+3 t$
  We can use the first equation to find the value of $w$ in terms of $t$:
  $w=7-2t$
  Substituting this value of $w$ in the second equation:
  $4(7-2t)+5t=25\quad \Rightarrow\quad 28-3t=25\quad \Rightarrow\quad t=1$
  Substituting this value of $t$ in the first equation:
  $w+2(1)=7\quad \Rightarrow\quad w=5$
  Finally, we can find the value of $2w+3t$:
  $2(5)+3(1)=13$
  Therefore, the answer is C: 13.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We are given two equations and two variables.
  We can solve for one of the variables in terms of the other in one of the equations.
  We can then substitute this expression into the other equation to solve for the other variable.
  Once we know the values of both variables, we can find the value of $2w+3t$ by plugging them in.
  
Action: 
  Subtracting the first equation from the second equation gives:
  $$(4w+5t)-(2w+4t)=25-14$$
  Simplifying the left side gives:
  $$2w+t=11$$
  Solving this equation for $t$ in terms of $w$ gives:
  $$t=11-2w$$
  Substituting this expression into the first equation gives:
  $$2w+4(11-2w)=14$$
  Simplifying and solving for $w$ gives:
  $$w=3$$
  Substituting this value of $w$ into the equation we found earlier gives:
  $$t=11-2(3)=5$$
  Finally, substituting these values of $w$ and $t$ into $2w+3t$ gives:
  $$2(3)+3(5)=6+15=21$$
  Therefore, the value of $2w+3t$ is 21.
  The answer is D: 17.
Response 2:
Thought:
  We have two equations with two variables.

Question: $$(a x+3)\left(5 x^{2}-b x+4\right)=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$The equation above is true for all $x$, where $a$ and $b$ are constants. What is the value of $a b$ ?
Choices:
  A: 18
  B: 20
  C: 24
  D: 40
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to find the value of $ab$.
  Let's simplify the given equation.
  $$(a x+3)\left(5 x^{2}-b x+4\right)=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$
  $$\Rightarrow 5ax^3 - abx^2 + 20ax^2 - 3bx + 15x^2 - 4a x + 12 = 20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$
  $$\Rightarrow 5ax^3 - abx^2 + 20ax^2 - 3bx + 15x^2 - 4a x = 20 x^{3}-24 x^{2}-2 x$$
  $$\Rightarrow 5ax^3 + (20a - 15)x^2 + (-ab + 4a + 3b)x - 20x^3 - 2x = -24x^2$$
  $$\Rightarrow -15ax^3 + (20a - 39)x^2 + (-ab + 4a + 3b - 2)x = 0$$
  Since the equation is true for all $x$, the coefficients of each power of $x$ must be equal to zero.
  Therefore, we get three equations from the above equation as follows:
  $$-15a = 0 \Rightarrow a = 0$$
  $$20a - 39 = 0 \Rightarrow a = \frac{39}{20}$$
  $$-ab + 4a + 3b - 2 = 0$$
  Substituting $a = \frac{39}{20}$ in the third equation, we get:
  $$-\frac{39b}{20} + \frac{156}{20} + 3b - 2 = 0$$
  $$\Rightarrow \frac{21b}{20} = \frac{4}{5}$$
  $$\Rightarrow b = \frac{16}{21}$$
  Therefore, $ab = \frac{39}{20} \times \frac{16}{21} = \frac{8}{5}$
  The answer is not in the choices. So, the most likely answer is "None of the Above".
  Therefore, the answer is None of the Above.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 15 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $a^{2}+b^{2}=z$ and $a b=y$, which of the following is equivalent to $4 z+8 y$ ?
Choices:
  A: $(a+2 b)^{2}$
  B: $(2 a+2 b)^{2}$
  C: $(4 a+4 b)^{2}$
  D: $(4 a+8 b)^{2}$
Response 0:
Thought:
We are given that $a^{2}+b^{2}=z$ and $ab=y$. We need to simplify $4z+8y$ using these expressions.
We can factorize $4z+8y$ as $4(z+2y)$.
We can substitute $z=a^{2}+b^{2}$ and $y=ab$ in the expression $4(z+2y)$ to get $4(a^{2}+b^{2}+2ab)$.
We can then simplify $4(a^{2}+b^{2}+2ab)$ as $4(a+b)^{2}$.
Therefore, the answer is C: $(4 a+4 b)^{2}$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
We are given that $a^2+b^2=z$ and $ab=y$.
We want to simplify $4z+8y$ using the given information.
We can rewrite $4z+8y$ as $4(a^2+b^2)+8(ab)$.
We can factor out a 4 from this expression to get $4(a^2+2ab+b^2)$.
We recognize that $a^2+2ab+b^2$ is the square of the sum of $a$ and $b$, which is $(a+b)^2$.
Therefore, $4(a^2+2ab+b^2)=4(a+b)^2$.
Thus, $4z+8y=4(a+b)^2$.
The answer is B: $(2a+2b)^2$.

Action: Answer("B")

  $=4(a^{2}+2 a b+b^{2})$

Topic: Math
Question: Shipping Charges\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$\begin{array}{c}\text { Merchandise weight } \\ \text { (pounds) }\end{array}$ & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Shipping } \\ \text { charge }\end{array}$ \\\hline5 & $\$ 16.94$ \\\hline10 & $\$ 21.89$ \\\hline20 & $\$ 31.79$ \\\hline40 & $\$ 51.59$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows shipping charges for an online retailer that sells sporting goods. There is a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise. Which function can be used to determine the total shipping charge $f(x)$, in dollars, for an order with a merchandise weight of $x$ pounds?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=0.99 x$
  B: $f(x)=0.99 x+11.99$
  C: $f(x)=3.39 x$
  D: $f(x)=3.39 x+16.94$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  There is a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise.
  The function for a linear relationship is $f(x) = mx + b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  We can use the given data to calculate the slope and y-intercept of the function.
  Using the two points $(5,16.94)$ and $(10,21.89)$, we can calculate the slope: $m = \frac{21.89-16.94}{10-5} = 0.99$.
  Using the point $(5,16.94)$ and the slope $m=0.99$, we can solve for the y-intercept: $16.94 = 0.99 \cdot 5 + b$, which gives $b = 11.99$.
  Therefore, the function that can be used to determine the total shipping charge $f(x)$, in dollars, for an order with a merchandise weight of $x$ pounds is $f(x) = 0.99x + 11.99$.
  The answer is B: $f(x)=0.99 x+11.99$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The function is linear and can be represented in slope-intercept form as $f(x)=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  The slope of the function is the rate of change of the shipping charge per pound of merchandise weight.
  The y-intercept is the shipping charge when the merchandise weight is 0 pounds.
  Using the given table, we can calculate the slope of the function as follows:
  slope $m = \frac{\text{change in y}}{\text{change in x}} = \frac{\$21.89 - \$16.94}{10 - 5} = \frac{\$4.95}{5} = \$0.99$
  Therefore, the function is $f(x)=0.99x+b$.
  To find the y-intercept, we can use any point in the table. Using the first row, we get:
  $16.94 = 0.99(5) + b$
  $b = 11.99$
  Therefore, the function is $f(x)=0.99x+11.99$.
  The answer is B.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 18 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $a$ & $3 a$ & $5 a$ \\\hline$y$ & 0 & $-a$ & $-2 a$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of $x$ and their corresponding values of $y$ are shown in the table above, where $a$ is a constant. If there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, which of the following equations represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $x+2 y=a$
  B: $x+2 y=5 a$
  C: $2 x-y=-5 a$
  D: $2 x-y=7 a$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  To determine the linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, we need to use the formula for the equation of a line: $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope of the line and $b$ is the y-intercept. 
  We can find the slope of the line using two points from the table. 
  For example, using the points $(a,0)$ and $(3a,-a)$, the slope is $m=\frac{-a-0}{3a-a}=-\frac{1}{2}$. 
  We can then use the slope and one of the points to find the y-intercept. 
  Using the point $(a,0)$, we have $0=-\frac{1}{2}a+b$, so $b=\frac{1}{2}a$. 
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $y=-\frac{1}{2}x+\frac{1}{2}a$. 
  Multiplying both sides by 2, we get $2y=-x+a$, which is equivalent to $2x-y=a$. 
  Therefore, the answer is D: $2x-y=7a$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& g(x)=2 x-1 \\& h(x)=1-g(x)\end{aligned}$$The functions $g$ and $h$ are defined above. What is the value of $h(0)$ ?
Choices:
  A: -2
  B: 0
  C: 1
  D: 2
Response 0:
Thought:
  We are given the functions $g(x)$ and $h(x)$.
  We are asked to find $h(0)$.
  We know that $h(x) = 1 - g(x)$.
  We know that $g(x) = 2x - 1$.
  Therefore, $h(x) = 1 - (2x - 1) = 2 - 2x$.
  To find $h(0)$, we substitute $x=0$ into $h(x)$.
  Therefore, $h(0) = 2 - 2(0) = 2$.
  The answer is D: 2.

Question: A circle in the $x y$-plane has center $(5,7)$ and radius 2. Which of the following is an equation of the circle?
Choices:
  A: $(x-5)^{2}+(y-7)^{2}=4$
  B: $(x+5)^{2}+(y+7)^{2}=4$
  C: $(x-5)^{2}+(y-7)^{2}=2$
  D: $(x+5)^{2}+(y+7)^{2}=2$

  Therefore, the equation of the circle is $(x-5)^2 + (y-7)^2 = 2^2$.

Question: On Saturday afternoon, Armand sent $m$ text messages each hour for 5 hours, and Tyrone sent $p$ text messages each hour for 4 hours. Which of the following represents the total number of messages sent by Armand and Tyrone on Saturday afternoon?

  B: $20 m p$
  C: $5 m+4 p$

Question: A psychologist set up an experiment to study the tendency of a person to select the first item when presented with a series of items. In the experiment, 300 people were presented with a set of five pictures arranged in random order. Each person was asked to choose the most appealing picture. Of the first 150 participants, 36 chose the first picture in the set. Among the remaining 150 participants, $p$ people chose the first picture in the set. If more than $20 \%$ of all participants chose the first picture in the set, which of the following inequalities best describes the possible values of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: $p>0.20(300-36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  B: $p>0.20(300+36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  C: $p-36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
  D: $p+36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The total number of participants is 300.
  Among the first 150 participants, 36 chose the first picture.
  This means that $0.24$ or $24\%$ of the first 150 participants chose the first picture.
  We are looking for a possible range of values of $p$ such that more than $20 \%$ of all participants chose the first picture.
  This means that $0.20(300) = 60$ or more participants must choose the first picture.
  We know that 36 participants from the first 150 chose the first picture, so we need at least $60-36=24$ participants from the remaining 150 to choose the first picture.
  Therefore, $p$ must be greater than 24.
  The answer is C: $p-36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$.
Action: Answer("C")

Question: Which of the following is an equivalent form of $(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}-\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right) ?$
Choices:
  A: $-2.2 x^{2}+1.6$
  B: $-2.2 x^{2}+11.2$
  C: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$
  D: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+0.64$
Response 0:
Thought:
We can simplify the given expression by first expanding $(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}$ and then subtracting $(5.2 x^{2}-6.4)$ from it.
$(1.5 x-2.4)^{2} = (1.5 x)^2 - 2 \cdot 1.5 x \cdot 2.4 + (2.4)^2 = 2.25 x^2 - 7.2 x + 5.76$
Subtracting $(5.2 x^{2}-6.4)$ from $(2.25 x^2 - 7.2 x + 5.76)$, we get $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$.
Therefore, the answer is C: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 26 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In the $x y$-plane, the line determined by the points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ passes through the origin. Which of the following could be the value of $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 4
  C: 8
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought:
  The line passes through the origin. Therefore, the line passes through the point $(0,0)$.
  If the line passes through $(0,0)$, then both $(2,k)$ and $(k,32)$ must lie on the same line that passes through $(0,0)$.
  We can use the slope of the line to determine which values of $k$ satisfy the condition.
  The slope of the line is $\frac{32- k}{k-2}$.
  If $(2,k)$ and $(k,32)$ lie on the same line that passes through $(0,0)$, then the slope of the line is $\frac{k-32}{-k}$.
  Therefore, $\frac{32- k}{k-2} = \frac{k-32}{-k}$.
  Solving for $k$, we get $k = -8$ or $k = 16$.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 16.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  If the line passes through the origin, then the line must have an intercept of 0.
  The equation of the line passing through the two points is given by: $y - k = \frac{32-k}{k-2}(x-k)$.
  If the line passes through the origin, then $k=0$ or $k=4$.
  If $k=0$, then the two points are $(2,0)$ and $(0,32)$, which lie on the $x$ and $y$-axes, respectively.
  If $k=4$, then the two points are $(2,4)$ and $(4,32)$, and the line passes through $(0,0)$.
  Therefore, the possible values of $k$ are 0 and 4.
  The answer is either A: 0 or B: 4.

  If the line passes through the origin, then the points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ must be on the same line as the origin.
  The slope of the line through $(2,k)$ and $(k,32)$ is $\frac{32-k}{k-2}$.
  If the line passes through the origin, then the slope of the line is also $\frac{32}{k}$.
  Therefore, $\frac{32-k}{k-2}=\frac{32}{k}$.
  Multiplying both sides by $k(k-2)$ gives $32k-2k^2=64-32k$, which simplifies to $2k^2-32k+64=0$.
  Factoring gives $2(k-8)^2=0$, which means $k=8$.
Action: Answer("C")

Question: If 50 one-cent coins were stacked on top of each other in a column, the column would be approximately $3 \frac{7}{8}$ inches tall. At this rate, which of the following is closest to the number of one-cent coins it would take to make an 8-inch-tall column?
Choices:
  A: 75
  B: 100
  C: 200
  D: 390
Response 0:
Thought:
  50 coins stack up to a height of $3 \frac{7}{8}$ inches.
  We can find the height of one coin by dividing $3 \frac{7}{8}$ by 50.
  One coin has a height of $\frac{3 \frac{7}{8}}{50} = 0.0775$ inches.
  To find the number of coins needed to make an 8-inch-tall column, we divide 8 by 0.0775.
  $\frac{8}{0.0775} \approx 103.22$, which is closest to 100.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 100.

  B: 6,027

  If we let $r$ be the rate of increase in inches per year, then the diameter of each tree after 10 years will be $12 + 10r$ inches.
  The difference in their diameters after 10 years will be $(12 + 10r) - (12 + 10r) = 10r$ inches.
  To find $r$, we need to use the fact that the diameter of a tree is proportional to the square root of its age.
  If $d$ is the diameter of a tree in inches and $a$ is its age in years, then we can write $d = k\sqrt{a}$ for some constant $k$.
  Since the diameter of each tree is 12 inches when its age is 1 year, we have $12 = k\sqrt{1}$, so $k = 12$.
  Therefore, the diameter of each tree after $a$ years is $d = 12\sqrt{a}$ inches.
  After 10 years, the diameter of each tree will be $d = 12\sqrt{10}$ inches.
  The difference in their diameters after 10 years will be $10\left(12\sqrt{10} - 12\sqrt{10}\right) = 0$ inches.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 1.0.

Question: A company purchased a machine valued at $\$ 120,000$. The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year so that after 10 years the value will be $\$ 30,000$. Which of the following equations gives the value, $v$, of the machine, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased for $0 \leq t \leq 10 ?$
Choices:
  A: $v=30,000-9,000 t$
  B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$
  C: $v=120,000+9,000 t$
  D: $v=120,000-30,000 t$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The machine depreciates by the same amount each year.
  After 10 years, the value of the machine will be $\$ 30,000$.
  The initial value of the machine is $\$ 120,000$.
  Let $d$ be the amount of depreciation per year.
  Then, the value of the machine after $t$ years is $v=120,000-dt$.
  We can solve for $d$ using the given information: $30,000=120,000-10d$, so $d=9,000$.
  Therefore, the equation that gives the value of the machine, $v$, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased is $v=120,000-9,000t$.
  The answer is B: $v=120,000-9,000t$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:

  The value of the machine after $t$ years is $v$.
  Therefore, $v = 120,000 - dt$.
  We need to find the value of $d$.
  From the information given, we know that $v = 30,000$ when $t = 10$.
  Plugging these values into the equation, we get $30,000 = 120,000 - d(10)$.
  Solving for $d$, we get $d = 9,000$.
  Substituting this value of $d$ into the equation, we get $v = 120,000 - 9,000t$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $v=30,000-9,000t$.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 37 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& x=y-3 \\& \frac{x}{2}+2 y=6\end{aligned}$$Which ordered pair $(x, y)$ satisfies the system of equations shown above?
Choices:
  A: $(-3,0)$
  B: $(0,3)$
  C: $(6,-3)$
  D: $(36,-6)$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We have two equations and two variables.
  We can use substitution or elimination method to solve the system of equations.
  Let's use substitution method to solve the system of equations.
  We are given that $x = y - 3$.
  We can substitute this value of x in the second equation and solve for y.
  Once we have the value of y, we can substitute it back in the first equation and solve for x.
  The ordered pair that satisfies both equations is the solution.
  
Action: Answer("A") $(-3,0)$ 

Solution:
  Substituting $x = y - 3$ in the second equation, we get:
  $$\frac{y-3}{2} + 2y = 6$$
  $$\frac{y}{2} - \frac{3}{2} + 2y = 6$$
  $$\frac{5y}{2} = \frac{15}{2}$$
  $$y = 3$$
  Now, substituting $y = 3$ in the first equation, we get:
  $$x = 3 - 3$$
  $$x = 0$$
  Therefore, the ordered pair that satisfies the system of equations is $(x,y) = (-3,0)$.
  So, the answer is A: $(-3,0)$.

  We can substitute y=3 into the first equation and solve for x.
  $$\begin{aligned} & x=y-3 \\ \Rightarrow & x=3-3 \\ \Rightarrow & x=0 \end{aligned}$$
  Therefore, the ordered pair $(x,y)$ that satisfies the system of equations is $(0,3)$.
  The answer is B: $(0,3)$.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 38 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Ken is working this summer as part of a crew on a farm. He earned $\$ 8$ per hour for the first 10 hours he worked this week. Because of his performance, his crew leader raised his salary to $\$ 10$ per hour for the rest of the week. Ken saves $90 \%$ of his earnings from each week. What is the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week?
Choices:
  A: 38
  B: 33
  C: 22
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Ken earned $\$ 8$ per hour for the first $10$ hours he worked, so he earned $\$ 8 \cdot 10 = \$ 80$ in the first $10$ hours.
  Let $x$ be the number of hours Ken needs to work the rest of the week.
  He earns $\$ 10$ per hour for the remaining $x$ hours he works.
  He saves $90 \%$ of his earnings, so he saves $\$ 0.9 \cdot (\$ 80 + \$ 10x) = \$ 72 + \$ 9x$ for the week.
  We need to solve the inequality $\$ 72 + \$ 9x \geq \$ 270$ to find the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week.
  Simplifying the inequality gives $x \geq 22$.
  Therefore, the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week is $22$.
  The answer is C: 22.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
- Ken earned $8 \times 10 = 80$ dollars for the first 10 hours of work.
- Let $x$ be the number of hours he works for the rest of the week.
- For each of these hours, he earns $10$ dollars.
- Therefore, he earns $10x$ dollars for the rest of the week.
- Ken saves $90 \%$ of his earnings, so he saves $0.9(80 + 10x)$ dollars for the week.
- We want to find the least $x$ such that $0.9(80 + 10x) \ge 270$.
- Simplifying the inequality gives $x \ge 19$.
- The least integer value of $x$ that satisfies the inequality is $x = 20$.
- Therefore, Ken must work at least $10 + 20 = 30$ hours this week to save at least $\$ 270$.
- The answer is not one of the choices.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Ken earned $\$8$ per hour for the first 10 hours he worked this week, which is $\$8 \times 10 = \$80$.
  The remaining amount of money he needs to earn is $\$270 - \$80 = \$190$.
  Ken saves $90 \%$ of his earnings from each week, so he keeps $100 \% - 90 \% = 10 \%$ of his earnings.
  The amount of money he needs to earn before savings is $\frac{\$190}{10 \%} = \$1900$.
  He worked for 10 hours with a rate of $\$8$ per hour, so he earned $\$80$.
  The remaining amount of money he needs to earn is $\$1900 - \$80 = \$1820$.
  He earns $\$10$ per hour for the remaining hours he works.
  The number of hours he needs to work is $\frac{\$1820}{\$10} = 182$.

$\$ 10 \text{ per hour} \cdot h \geq \$ 220$

Dividing both sides by $\$ 10 \text{ per hour}$:
$h \geq 22$

Therefore, Ken must work at least 22 hours for the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week.

Question: A cargo helicopter delivers only 100-pound packages and 120-pound packages. For each delivery trip, the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages, and the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds. What is the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 4
  C: 5
  D: 6
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's assume that the helicopter carries 'x' 100-pound packages and 'y' 120-pound packages.
  The helicopter must carry at least 10 packages, so x + y >= 10.
  The total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds, so 100x + 120y <= 1,100.
  We need to find the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip.
  We can solve this problem by using trial and error method.
  If we start with option D, then the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry is 6.
  If we carry 6 120-pound packages, then the weight of these packages is 6*120 = 720 pounds.
  The remaining weight for 100-pound packages is 1,100 - 720 = 380 pounds.
  The maximum number of 100-pound packages that can be carried is 380/100 = 3.8.
  But the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages, so we cannot carry 3.8 packages.
  If we carry 3 100-pound packages, then the weight of these packages is 3*100 = 300 pounds.
  The remaining weight for 120-pound packages is 1,100 - 300 = 800 pounds.
  The maximum number of 120-pound packages that can be carried is 800/120 = 6.66.
  But we cannot carry 6.66 packages.
  Therefore, the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip is less than 6.
  If we try option C, then the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry is 5.
  If we carry 5 120-pound packages, then the weight of these packages is 5*120 = 600 pounds.
  The remaining weight for 100-pound packages is 1,100 - 600 = 500 pounds.
  The maximum number of 100-pound packages that can be carried is 500/100 = 5.
  The total number of packages carried is 5 + 5 = 10.
  Therefore, the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip is 5.
  The answer is C: 5.

What is the meaning of the value 108 in this equation?
Choices:
  A: Kathy will complete the repairs within 108 days.
  B: Kathy starts each week with 108 phones to fix.
  C: Kathy repairs phones at a rate of 108 per hour.
  D: Kathy repairs phones at a rate of 108 per day.

  A: $-14-18 i$
  B: $-4-6 i$
  C: $4+6 i$
  D: $14+18 i$

  By substituting $i^{2}=-1$ in the given expression, we get:
  $(5+12i)-\left(9(-1)-6i\right)$
  Simplifying this expression, we get:
  $5+12i+9+6i$
  $=14+18i$
  Therefore, the answer is D: $14+18i$.

Question: In the $x y$-plane, the parabola with equation $y=(x-11)^{2}$ intersects the line with equation $y=25$ at two points, $A$ and $B$. What is the length of $\overline{A B}$ ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 12
  C: 14
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to find the x-coordinates of the points A and B where the parabola intersects the line y=25.
  We can set the two equations equal to each other to solve for the x-coordinates of the intersection points.
  $(x-11)^2 = 25$
  Taking the square root of both sides, we get $x-11 = \pm 5$
  Solving for x, we get $x=6$ and $x=16$.
  Therefore, the length of $\overline{A B}$ is $16-6=10$.
  The answer is A: 10.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The equation of the parabola is $y=(x-11)^2$.
  The equation of the line is $y=25$.
  To find the $x$-coordinates of the points of intersection, we set the two equations equal to each other and solve for $x$.
  $(x-11)^2=25$
  Taking the square root of both sides, we get $x-11=\pm5$.
  So $x=6$ or $x=16$.
  Therefore, the $x$-coordinates of points $A$ and $B$ are 6 and 16.
  The $y$-coordinate of both points is 25, since they lie on the line $y=25$.
  So, the distance between $A$ and $B$ is the difference between their $x$-coordinates, which is $16-6=10$.
  Therefore, the length of $\overline{A B}$ is 10.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 46 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Oil and gas production in a certain area dropped from 4 million barrels in 2000 to 1.9 million barrels in 2013. Assuming that the oil and gas production decreased at a constant rate, which of the following linear functions $f$ best models the production, in millions of barrels, $t$ years after the year 2000 ?
Choices:
  A: $f(t)=\frac{21}{130} t+4$
  B: $f(t)=\frac{19}{130} t+4$
  C: $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130} t+4$
  D: $f(t)=-\frac{19}{130} t+4$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The oil and gas production dropped from 4 million barrels in 2000 to 1.9 million barrels in 2013.
  The difference in production is $4-1.9=2.1$ million barrels.
  The time elapsed is $2013-2000=13$ years.
  Therefore, the rate of decrease is $\frac{2.1}{13}= \frac{21}{130}$ million barrels per year.
  Since the production is decreasing, the slope of the linear function is negative.
  Therefore, the function that models the production should have a negative slope.
  The function should pass through the point $(0,4)$ since the production was 4 million barrels in 2000.
  The only function that satisfies all these conditions is $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130} t+4$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We can use the slope-intercept form of a linear function: $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  The production decreased from 4 million barrels in 2000 to 1.9 million barrels in 2013, which is a decrease of 2.1 million barrels over 13 years. 
  The slope of the linear function is the rate of change of production per year. 
  The slope is the change in production over the change in time, which is $\frac{-2.1}{13}=-\frac{21}{130}$.
  The y-intercept is the initial production in the year 2000, which is 4 million barrels.
  Therefore, the linear function that models the production is $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130}t+4$.

Question: The formula below is often used by project managers to compute $E$, the estimated time to complete a job, where $O$ is the shortest completion time, $P$ is the longest completion time, and $M$ is the most likely completion time.$$E=\frac{O+4 M+P}{6}$$Which of the following correctly gives $P$ in terms of $E, O$, and $M$ ?
Choices:
  A: $P=6 E-O-4 M$
  B: $P=-6 E+O+4 M$
  C: $P=\frac{O+4 M+E}{6}$
  D: $P=\frac{O+4 M-E}{6}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  To solve for $P$, we need to isolate $P$ on one side of the equation.
  Multiply both sides of the equation by 6.
  Distribute the multiplication on the right-hand side.
  Isolate $P$ on one side of the equation.
  The correct answer should be the equation that gives $P$ in terms of $E, O,$ and $M$.
  
Action: Answer("A") 
Solution:
  Multiply both sides of the equation by 6:
  $$6E=O+4M+P$$
  Isolate $P$ on one side of the equation:
  $$P=6E-O-4M$$
  The correct answer is A: $P=6E-O-4M$.

Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $f(x)$ \\\hline1 & 5 \\\hline3 & 13 \\\hline5 & 21 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of the linear function $f$ are shown in the table above. Which of the following defines $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=2 x+3$
  B: $f(x)=3 x+2$
  C: $f(x)=4 x+1$
  D: $f(x)=5 x$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The function $f$ is linear.
  We can use the slope-intercept form of a linear equation to find the equation for $f$.
  The slope of the line passing through the points $(1,5)$ and $(3,13)$ is $\frac{13-5}{3-1}=4$.
  The $y$-intercept of the line is $(0,f(0))=(0,3)$.
  Therefore, the equation for $f$ is $f(x)=4x+3$.
  The answer is not any of the given choices.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  To find the equation of a line, we need to find the slope and y-intercept.
  Slope is the change in y over the change in x.
  Slope $m = \frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x} = \frac{f(x_2)-f(x_1)}{x_2-x_1}$.
  Using the table, we can find two points on the line: $(1,5)$ and $(5,21)$.
  Slope $m = \frac{f(5)-f(1)}{5-1} = \frac{21-5}{4} = 4$.
  We can use point-slope form to find the equation of the line: $y - y_1 = m(x - x_1)$.
  Using point $(1,5)$, we get $y - 5 = 4(x - 1)$.
  Simplifying, we get $y = 4x + 1$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $f(x)=4 x+1$.
Action: Answer("C")

  To find the value of $b$, we can use any of the given points. Let's use $(1,5)$.
  Substituting $x=1$ and $y=5$ into the equation, we get $5=4(1)+b$, which gives $b=1$.
  Therefore, the equation of the linear function is $f(x)=4x+1$.
  The answer is C: $f(x)=4 x+1$.

Question: Dreams Recalled during One Week\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|c|c|}\hline& None & 1 to 4 & 5 or more & Total \\\hline\hlineGroup X & 15 & 28 & 57 & 100 \\\hlineGroup Y & 21 & 11 & 68 & 100 \\\hlineTotal & 36 & 39 & 125 & 200 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The data in the table above were produced by a sleep researcher studying the number of dreams people recall when asked to record their dreams for one week. Group X consisted of 100 people who observed early bedtimes, and Group Y consisted of 100 people who observed later bedtimes. If a person is chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream, what is the probability that the person belonged to Group Y ?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{68}{100}$
  B: $\frac{79}{100}$
  C: $\frac{79}{164}$
  D: $\frac{164}{200}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We want to find the probability of a person belonged to Group Y given that the person recalled at least 1 dream.
  The probability of a person recalled at least 1 dream is $\frac{39+125}{200}= \frac{164}{200}$.
  The probability that a person belonged to Group Y and recalled at least 1 dream is $\frac{68}{200}$.
  Therefore, the probability that the person belonged to Group Y given that the person recalled at least 1 dream is:
  \begin{align*}
  P(\text{Group Y}|\text{Recalled at least 1 dream}) &= \frac{P(\text{Group Y and Recalled at least 1 dream})}{P(\text{Recalled at least 1 dream})} \\
  &= \frac{\frac{68}{200}}{\frac{164}{200}} \\
  &= \frac{17}{41}
  \end{align*}
  So the answer is C: $\frac{79}{164}$.
Action: Answer("C")

  The total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream is 28 + 57 + 11 + 68 = 164.
  The number of people in Group Y who recalled at least 1 dream is 11 + 68 = 79.
  Therefore, the probability that a person chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream belonged to Group Y is 79/164.

The horse with the lowest reported weight was found to actually weigh 10 pounds less than its reported weight. What value remains unchanged if the four values are reported using the corrected weight?
Choices:
  A: Mean
  B: Median
  C: Range
  D: Standard deviation
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The mean, median, range, and standard deviation are all measures of central tendency or dispersion of a dataset.
  The mean and standard deviation are affected by outliers and changes in the dataset.
  The median and range are not affected by outliers as they are based on the order of the data.
  Since only one value in the dataset is being changed, the median and range will stay the same.
  The standard deviation will change since it is affected by the values in the dataset.
  The mean will also change since it is affected by the values in the dataset.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Mean.

Question: What value of $x$ satisfies the equation $3 x+3=27$ ?
Choices:
  A: 3
  B: 8
  C: 10
  D: 27

  $3x + 3 - 3 = 27 - 3$
  $3x = 24$
  We can then solve for $x$ by dividing both sides of the equation by 3.
  $x = 8$
  Therefore, the value of $x$ that satisfies the equation is 8.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 55 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Keith modeled the growth over several hundred years of a tree population by estimating the number of the trees' pollen grains per square centimeter that were deposited each year within layers of a lake's sediment. He estimated there were 310 pollen grains per square centimeter the first year the grains were deposited, with a $1 \%$ annual increase in the number of grains per square centimeter thereafter. Which of the following functions models $P(t)$, the number of pollen grains per square centimeter $t$ years after the first year the grains were deposited?
Choices:
  A: $P(t)=310^{t}$
  B: $P(t)=310^{1.01 t}$
  C: $P(t)=310(0.99)^{t}$
  D: $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Each year, the number of pollen grains per square centimeter increases by $1 \%$.
  This means the amount of pollen grains per square centimeter is multiplied by $1.01$ each year.
  Keith estimated there were 310 pollen grains per square centimeter the first year.
  Therefore, the function that models the number of pollen grains per square centimeter $t$ years after the first year the grains were deposited is $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$.
  The answer is D: $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$.

Choices:
  A: The means are the same, and the standard deviations are different.
  B: The means are the same, and the standard deviations are the same.
  C: The means are different, and the standard deviations are different.
  D: The means are different, and the standard deviations are the same.
Response 0:
Thought:
  To compare the means and standard deviations of two lists, we need to calculate them.
  The mean of list A is $\frac{1+2+3+4+5+6}{6}=3.5$.
  The mean of list B is $\frac{2+3+3+4+4+5}{6}=3.5$.
  The standard deviation of list A is $\sqrt{\frac{(1-3.5)^2+(2-3.5)^2+(3-3.5)^2+(4-3.5)^2+(5-3.5)^2+(6-3.5)^2}{6}}\approx1.71$.

  The mean of both lists is the same, but the standard deviations are different.
  Therefore, the answer is A: The means are the same, and the standard deviations are different.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 57 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$C=75 h+125$$The equation above gives the amount $C$, in dollars, an electrician charges for a job that takes $h$ hours. Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland each hired this electrician. The electrician worked 2 hours longer on Ms. Sanchez's job than on Mr. Roland's job. How much more did the electrician charge Ms. Sanchez than Mr. Roland?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 75$
  B: $\$ 125$
  C: $\$ 150$
  D: $\$ 275$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's first find out how many hours the electrician worked for Mr. Roland's job.
  Let $h_1$ be the number of hours the electrician worked for Mr. Roland's job.
  Then, $h_1+2$ is the number of hours the electrician worked for Ms. Sanchez's job.
  We can set up two equations using the given information and solve for $C_1$ and $C_2$.
  $C_1 = 75h_1+125$
  $C_2 = 75(h_1+2)+125 = 75h_1+200$
  We want to find $C_2 - C_1$.
  $C_2 - C_1 = (75h_1+200)-(75h_1+125) = 75h_1+75$
  Therefore, the amount that the electrician charged more to Ms. Sanchez than to Mr. Roland is $\$75$.
  The answer is A: $\$75$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's start by finding out how much the electrician charged Mr. Roland.
  Let $h_{Roland}$ be the number of hours the electrician worked on Mr. Roland's job.
  Let $h_{Sanchez}$ be the number of hours the electrician worked on Ms. Sanchez's job.
  We know that $h_{Sanchez} = h_{Roland} + 2$, since the electrician worked 2 hours longer on Ms. Sanchez's job.
  We can use the equation $C=75h+125$ to find how much the electrician charged for each job.
  For Mr. Roland's job, $C_{Roland} = 75h_{Roland} + 125$.
  For Ms. Sanchez's job, $C_{Sanchez} = 75h_{Sanchez} + 125 = 75(h_{Roland} + 2) + 125 = 75h_{Roland} + 275$.
  Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $C_{Sanchez} - C_{Roland} = (75h_{Roland} + 275) - (75h_{Roland} + 125) = 150$ dollars more than Mr. Roland.
  The answer is C: $\$ 150$.
Action: Answer("C")

Thought:

  The amount the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez is $C=75(x+2)+125=75x+225$ dollars.
  The difference in the amount charged is $75x+225-(75x+125)=100$ dollars.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 58 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: Energy per Gram of Typical Macronutrients.\begin{center}.\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|}.\hline.Macronutrient & Food calories & Kilojoules \\.\hline.Protein & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.Fat & 9.0 & 37.7 \\.\hline.Carbohydrate & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.\end{tabular}.\end{center}.The table above gives the typical amounts of energy per gram, expressed in both food calories and kilojoules, of the three macronutrients in food.
Question: If the 180 food calories in a granola bar come entirely from $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate, which of the following expresses $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  C: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p-c)$
  D: $f=20+\frac{9}{4}(p+c)$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The energy in a granola bar is 180 food calories.
  The energy in a granola bar comes from protein, fat, and carbohydrate.
  The table gives the energy per gram of each macronutrient.
  Let $p$, $f$, and $c$ be the grams of protein, fat, and carbohydrate, respectively, in the granola bar.
  The energy in the granola bar from protein is $4p$ food calories.
  The energy in the granola bar from fat is $9f$ food calories.
  The energy in the granola bar from carbohydrate is $4c$ food calories.
  The total energy in the granola bar is $4p+9f+4c=180$.
  We want to express $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$.
  Solving for $f$ in the equation $4p+9f+4c=180$ gives $f=\frac{180-4p-4c}{9}$.
  Simplifying gives $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We know that the total food calories in a granola bar is 180.
  We also know that the energy per gram of protein is 4 food calories, the energy per gram of fat is 9 food calories, and the energy per gram of carbohydrate is 4 food calories.
  Therefore, we can set up the equation: $4p+9f+4c=180$.
  We want to solve for $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$.
  We can start by isolating $f$ on one side of the equation.
  We can do this by subtracting $4p$ and $4c$ from both sides: $9f=180-4p-4c$.
  Dividing both sides by 9, we get: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  The energy from $p$ grams of protein is $4p$ food calories.
  The energy from $f$ grams of fat is $9f$ food calories.
  The energy from $c$ grams of carbohydrate is $4c$ food calories.
  The total energy is 180 food calories.
  Therefore, $4p+9f+4c=180$.
  To solve for $f$, we need to isolate $f$ on one side of the equation.
  Subtracting $4p+4c$ from both sides of the equation yields $9f=180-4p-4c$.
  Dividing both sides by 9 gives $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.

Question: $$\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$$In the equation above, $k$ is a constant. If $x=9$, what is the value of $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 7
  C: 16
  D: 79

Thought:
  We can solve for k by substituting x=9 and then isolating k.
  If $\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$, then $\sqrt{k+2}=x$.
  Therefore, $k+2=x^2$.
  Substituting x=9, we get $k+2=9^2=81$.
  Solving for k, we get $k=81-2=79$.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 63 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: $$.a=1,052+1.08 t.$$.The speed of a sound wave in air depends on the air temperature. The formula above shows the relationship between $a$, the speed of a sound wave, in feet per second, and $t$, the air temperature, in degrees Fahrenheit $\left({ }^{\circ} \mathrm{F}\right)$.
Question: At which of the following air temperatures will the speed of a sound wave be closest to 1,000 feet per second?
Choices:
  A: $-46^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
  B: $-48^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
  C: $-49^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
  D: $-50^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to find the value of $t$ that makes $a$ closest to 1,000.
  We can calculate $a$ for each of the given values of $t$ and find the one that is closest to 1,000.
  We can use the absolute value of the difference between $a$ and 1,000 to determine which value of $t$ is closest to the desired value.
  Action: 
  Calculate $a$ for each value of $t$:
  For $t=-46^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$, $a=1,052+1.08(-46) \approx 1,000.32$.
  For $t=-48^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$, $a=1,052+1.08(-48) \approx 998.56$.
  For $t=-49^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$, $a=1,052+1.08(-49) \approx 997.68$.
  For $t=-50^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$, $a=1,052+1.08(-50) \approx 996.8$.
  The value of $t$ that makes $a$ closest to 1,000 is $t=-46^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$, since $|1,000.32-1,000|=0.32$ is the smallest of all the differences. 
  Therefore, the answer is A: $-46^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$. Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We need to find the value of $t$ that makes $a$ closest to 1000.
  We can find the value of $a$ for each choice of $t$ and choose the one that is closest to 1000.

Topic: Math
Question: $$2 a x-15=3(x+5)+5(x-1)$$In the equation above, $a$ is a constant. If no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, what is the value of $a$ ?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 2
  C: 4
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought:
  Simplifying the equation:
  $$2ax-15=3x+15+5x-5$$
  $$2ax-15=8x+10$$
  $$2ax=8x+25$$
  $$2ax-8x=25$$
  $$2x(a-4)=25$$
  $$x=\frac{25}{2(a-4)}$$
  For no value of x to satisfy the equation, the denominator must be equal to zero.
  $$a-4=0$$
  $$a=4$$
  Therefore, the answer is C: 4.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Simplifying the equation, we have:
  $$2ax-15=3x+15+5x-5$$
  $$2ax-15=8x+10$$
  $$2ax-8x=10+15$$
  $$x(2a-8)=25$$
  $$x=\frac{25}{2a-8}$$
  Since no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, the denominator of the fraction above must be zero. Therefore, we have:
  $$2a-8=0$$
  $$2a=8$$
  $$a=4$$
  The answer is C: 4.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 67 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The function $f$ is defined by $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$. The graph of $f$ in the $x y$-plane is a parabola. Which of the following intervals contains the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: $-4<x<-3$
  B: $-3<x<1$
  C: $1<x<3$
  D: $3<x<4$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  We can use the formula $x=-\frac{b}{2a}$ to find the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the parabola.
  The function $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$ can be expanded to $f(x)=x^2+4x+3$.
  The coefficient of the $x^2$ term is $a=1$, and the coefficient of the $x$ term is $b=4$.
  Therefore, the $x$-coordinate of the vertex is $x=-\frac{b}{2a}=-2$.
  The interval that contains $x=-2$ is $-3<x<1$.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $-3<x<1$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The vertex of a parabola with equation $y = a(x-h)^2+k$ is at $(h,k)$.
  The function $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$ can be written as $f(x)=x^2+4x+3$.
  This is a quadratic function in standard form, $y=ax^2+bx+c$ where $a=1$, $b=4$, and $c=3$.
  The $x$-coordinate of the vertex is given by $x=-\frac{b}{2a}$.
  Substituting the values for $a$ and $b$, we get $x=-\frac{4}{2(1)}=-2$.
  Therefore, the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of $f$ is $-2$.
  The interval that contains $-2$ is $-3<x<1$.
  The answer is B: $-3<x<1$.

  B: $-\frac{4}{5}$
  C: $-\frac{2}{3}$
  D: 4
Response 0:
Thought:

  Simplifying the left side gives $\frac{18x-12}{3}-4$
  Combining like terms on the left side gives $\frac{18x-16}{3}$
  Setting this equal to $9x-6$ gives $\frac{18x-16}{3}=9x-6$
  Multiplying both sides by 3 gives $18x-16=27x-18$
  Subtracting $18x$ from both sides gives $-16=9x-18$
  Adding 18 to both sides gives $2=9x$
  Dividing both sides by 9 gives $\frac{2}{9}=x$
  Substituting this into $3x-2$ gives $3(\frac{2}{9})-2$
  Simplifying gives $\frac{2}{3}-2$
  Combining like terms gives $-\frac{4}{3}$
  Therefore, the answer is C: $-\frac{2}{3}$.

Question: $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$Clayton will mix $x$ milliliters of a $10 \%$ by mass saline solution with $y$ milliliters of a $20 \%$ by mass saline solution in order to create an $18 \%$ by mass saline solution. The equation above represents this situation. If Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution, how many milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution must he use?
Choices:
  A: 5
  B: 25
  C: 50
  D: 100
Response 0:
Thought:
  We know that Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ saline solution.
  We need to find out how many milliliters of the $10 \%$ saline solution Clayton must use.
  We can use the given equation to solve for $x$.
  $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$
  $$0.10 x+0.20 (100)=0.18(x+100)$$
  $$0.10 x+20=0.18x+18$$
  $$0.08x=2$$
  $$x=25$$
  Therefore, Clayton must use 25 milliliters of the $10 \%$ saline solution.
  The answer is B: 25.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 70 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What are the solutions to $3 x^{2}+12 x+6=0 ?$
Choices:
  A: $x=-2 \pm \sqrt{2}$
  B: $x=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{30}}{3}$
  C: $x=-6 \pm \sqrt{2}$
  D: $x=-6 \pm 6 \sqrt{2}$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  We can find the solutions to the quadratic equation by using the quadratic formula: $x=\frac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^{2}-4 a c}}{2 a}$.
  Comparing the equation $3 x^{2}+12 x+6=0$ with the standard quadratic equation $a x^{2}+b x+c=0$, we have $a=3$, $b=12$, and $c=6$.
  Substituting the values into the quadratic formula, we get $x=\frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{12^{2}-4 \cdot 3 \cdot 6}}{2 \cdot 3}$.
  Simplifying, we get $x=\frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{96}}{6}$.
  Further simplifying, we get $x=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{24}}{3}$.
  Factoring out $\sqrt{24}$, we get $x=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{4 \cdot 6}}{3}$.
  Simplifying, we get $x=-2 \pm \frac{2 \sqrt{6}}{3}$.
  Therefore, the solutions are $x=-2 + \frac{2 \sqrt{6}}{3}$ and $x=-2 - \frac{2 \sqrt{6}}{3}$.
  The answer is B: $x=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{30}}{3}$.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 71 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Which of the following is equivalent to $2\left(x^{2}-x\right)+3\left(x^{2}-x\right) ?$
Choices:
  A: $5 x^{2}-5 x$
  B: $5 x^{2}+5 x$
  C: $5 x$
  D: $5 x^{2}$
Response 0:
Thought:
To simplify the given expression, we can combine like terms: 
$2\left(x^{2}-x\right)+3\left(x^{2}-x\right) = (2+3)x^2 - (2+3)x$
$= 5x^2 - 5x$
Therefore, the answer is A: $5 x^{2}-5 x$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Factor out $x^2 - x$ from both terms.
  $2\left(x^{2}-x\right)+3\left(x^{2}-x\right) = (2+3)(x^2 - x)$
  $= 5(x^2 - x)$
  $= 5x(x-1)$
  Therefore, the answer is C: $5x(x-1)$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Factor out $x^2-x$ from both terms.
  $2\left(x^{2}-x\right)+3\left(x^{2}-x\right) = (2+3)(x^2-x)$
  $= 5(x^2-x)$
  $= 5x(x-1)$
  Therefore, the answer is C: $5x(x-1)$.

Question: The graph of the exponential function $h$ in the $x y$-plane, where $y=h(x)$, has a $y$-intercept of $d$, where $d$ is a positive constant. Which of the following could define the function $h$ ?
Choices:
  A: $h(x)=-3(d)^{x}$
  B: $h(x)=3(x) d$
  C: $h(x)=d(-x)^{3}$
  D: $h(x)=d(3)^{x}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The $y$-intercept of the graph of $h$ is $d$, which means that when $x=0$, $y=d$.
  A: $h(x)=-3(d)^{x}$ is not an exponential function because the base is not a constant. Also, when $x=0$, $y=-3$, which is not equal to $d$.
  B: $h(x)=3(x) d$ is a linear function, not an exponential function. Also, when $x=0$, $y=0$, which is not equal to $d$.
  C: $h(x)=d(-x)^{3}$ is not an exponential function because the exponent is not a constant raised to the power of $x$. Also, when $x=0$, $y=d$, which is equal to the $y$-intercept.
  D: $h(x)=d(3)^{x}$ is an exponential function with base 3. Also, when $x=0$, $y=d$, which is equal to the $y$-intercept.
  Therefore, the answer is D: $h(x)=d(3)^{x}$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The $y$-intercept of a function is the point where the graph intersects the $y$-axis, which is when $x=0$.

  A: $h(0)=-3(d)^{0}=-3(1)=-3 \neq d$
  B: $h(0)=3(0)d=0 \neq d$
  C: $h(0)=d(-0)^{3}=0 \neq d$
  D: $h(0)=d(3)^{0}=d$
  Therefore, the function $h$ must be defined by $h(x)=d(3)^{x}$.
  The answer is D: $h(x)=d(3)^{x}$.

  B: Median
  C: Range

Question: A rectangle was altered by increasing its length by 10 percent and decreasing its width by $p$ percent. If these alterations decreased the area of the rectangle by 12 percent, what is the value of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: 12
  B: 15
  C: 20
  D: 22
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the original length and width of the rectangle are L and W, respectively.
  The original area of the rectangle is L * W.
  After the alterations, the new length and width of the rectangle are 1.1L and (1 - p/100)W, respectively.
  The new area of the rectangle is (1.1L) * (1 - p/100)W.
  We know that the new area is 0.88 times the original area, which means:
      (1.1L) * (1 - p/100)W = 0.88 * L * W
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
      1.1 * (1 - p/100) = 0.88
  Solving for p, we get:
      p = 20
  Therefore, the value of p is 20.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let the original length be $l$ and the original width be $w$.
The original area is $lw$.
After increasing the length by 10%, the new length is $1.1l$.
After decreasing the width by $p$%, the new width is $(1-\frac{p}{100})w$.
The new area is $(1-0.12)$ times the original area.
So we have the equation:
$$(1.1l) \cdot (1-\frac{p}{100})w = 0.88lw$$
Simplifying the equation, we get:
$$1.1(1-\frac{p}{100})=0.88$$
$$1-\frac{p}{100}=\frac{0.88}{1.1}$$
$$\frac{p}{100}=1-\frac{0.88}{1.1}$$
$$p=100(1-\frac{0.88}{1.1})$$
$$p=100(1-0.8)$$
$$p=20$$
Therefore, the value of $p$ is 20.

Topic: Math
Question: If $(a x+2)(b x+7)=15 x^{2}+c x+14$ for all values of $x$, and $a+b=8$, what are the two possible values for $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: 3 and 5
  B: 6 and 35
  C: 10 and 21
  D: 31 and 41
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can expand the left-hand side of the equation to get a quadratic equation in the form $Ax^2 + Bx + C$.
  Then we can compare the coefficients of the quadratic equation with the given quadratic equation to find the values of $a$, $b$, and $c$.
  We can then use the fact that $a + b = 8$ to solve for $a$ and $b$, and then substitute the values into the quadratic equation to find the possible values of $c$.
  Let's expand the left-hand side of the equation.
  
  $(a x+2)(b x+7) = abx^2 + (7a + 2b)x + 14$
  
  We can see that $c = 7a + 2b$.
  
  Now we can use the fact that $a + b = 8$ to solve for $a$ and $b$.
  
  $a = 8 - b$
  
  Substituting this into the equation for $c$, we get:
  
  $c = 7(8-b) + 2b = 54 - 5b$
  
  We want to find the two possible values of $c$, so we need to find the two possible values of $b$.
  
  Let's factor the quadratic equation on the right-hand side of the equation to find its roots.
  
  $(a x+2)(b x+7) = 15 x^{2}+c x+14$
  
  $(ax + 2)(bx + 7) - (15x^2 + cx + 14) = 0$
  
  $(ab - 15)x^2 + (7a + 2b - c)x - 14 = 0$
  
  The roots of this quadratic equation are the values of $x$ that make the equation true for all values of $x$.
  
  The roots of the equation are given by:
  
  $x = \frac{-B \pm \sqrt{B^2 - 4AC}}{2A}$
  
  $x = \frac{c - 7a - 2b \pm \sqrt{(7a + 2b - c)^2 - 4(ab - 15)(-14)}}{2(ab - 15)}$
  
  $x = \frac{c - 7a - 2b \pm \sqrt{(7a + 2b - c)^2 + 840(ab - 15)}}{2(ab - 15)}$
  
  For the equation to be true for all values of $x$, the discriminant must be equal to zero.
  
  $(7a + 2b - c)^2 + 840(ab - 15) = 0$
  
  Expanding this equation, we get:
  
  $49a^2 + 4b^2 + c^2 - 14ac - 28bc + 56ab = 0$
  
  Substituting $a = 8 - b$, we get:
  
  $49(8-b)^2 + 4b^2 + c^2 - 14c(8-b) - 28bc + 56(8-b)b = 0$
  
  Simplifying this equation, we get:
  
  $5b^2 - 26cb + c^2 + 448 = 0$
  
  This is a quadratic equation in $b$, and we can use the quadratic formula to find the two possible values of $b$.
  
  $b = \frac{26c \pm \sqrt{676c^2 - 4(5)(448)(c^2)}}{10}$
  
  $b = \frac{13c \pm \sqrt{169c^2 - 4480c^2}}{5}$
  
  $b = \frac{13c \pm \sqrt{-4311c^2}}{5}$
  
  Since $c$ is a real number, the discriminant is negative and the equation has no real roots.
  
  Therefore, there are no possible values for $c$.
  
  The answer is None of the Above.

Matching coefficients:
  $ab=15$
  $7a+2b=c$
  
Using the given condition:
  $a+b=8$
  $b=8-a$
  
Substituting into the first equation:
  $a(8-a)=15$
  $a^2-8a+15=0$
  $(a-3)(a-5)=0$
  $a=3$ or $a=5$

  $a=3$, $b=5$, $c=7a+2b=21+10=31$
  $a=5$, $b=3$, $c=7a+2b=35+6=41$
  
Therefore, the two possible values for $c$ are 31 and 41.

Question: What is the set of all solutions to the equation $\sqrt{x+2}=-x ?$
Choices:
  A: $\{-1,2\}$
  B: $\{-1\}$
  C: $\{2\}$
  D: There are no solutions to the given equation.
Response 0:
Thought:
To solve the given equation, we must first isolate the radical, then square both sides of the equation, and finally solve for $x$. 
$\sqrt{x+2}=-x$
$x+2=x^2$
$x^2-x-2=0$
$(x-2)(x+1)=0$
$x=2$ or $x=-1$
However, we must check our solutions since we squared both sides of the equation, which could have introduced extraneous roots.
Checking $x=2$: $\sqrt{2+2}=-2$ is false.
Checking $x=-1$: $\sqrt{-1+2}=1$ is true.
Therefore, the set of all solutions to the equation is $\{-1\}$.
The answer is B: $\{-1\}$. 
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We need to solve the equation $\sqrt{x+2}=-x$.
  Since the square root of a number is always non-negative, we must have $-x\geq 0$.
  Therefore, $x\leq 0$.
  Squaring both sides of the equation $\sqrt{x+2}=-x$, we get $x+2=x^2$.
  Rearranging the terms, we get $x^2-x-2=0$.
  Factoring the quadratic equation, we get $(x-2)(x+1)=0$.
  Therefore, the solutions to the equation are $x=2$ and $x=-1$.
  However, $x=-1$ is not a valid solution since it does not satisfy the original equation. 
  Therefore, the set of all solutions to the equation $\sqrt{x+2}=-x$ is $\{2\}$.
  The answer is C: $\{2\}$.

Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|}\hline\multicolumn{3}{|c|}{Townsend Realty Group Investments} \\\hlineProperty address & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Purchase price } \\ \text { (dollars) }\end{array}$ & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Monthly rental } \\ \text { price } \\ \text { (dollars) }\end{array}$ \\\hlineClearwater Lane & 128,000 & 950 \\\hlineDriftwood Drive & 176,000 & 1,310 \\\hlineEdgemont Street & 70,000 & 515 \\\hlineGlenview Street & 140,000 & 1,040 \\\hlineHamilton Circle & 450,000 & 3,365 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The Townsend Realty Group invested in the five different properties listed in the table above. The table shows the amount, in dollars, the company paid for each property and the corresponding monthly rental price, in dollars, the company charges for the property at each of the five locations. 23The relationship between the monthly rental price $r$, in dollars, and the property's purchase price $p$, in thousands of dollars, can be represented by a linear function. Which of the following functions represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $r(p)=2.5 p-870$
  B: $r(p)=5 p+165$
  C: $r(p)=6.5 p+440$
  D: $r(p)=7.5 p-10$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We are looking for a linear function that represents the relationship between the monthly rental price and the property's purchase price.
  The function should be in the form of $r(p) = mp + b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  We can use two points from the table to find the slope of the function.
  Let's use the points $(128, 950)$ and $(176, 1310)$.
  The slope is $m = \frac{1310 - 950}{176 - 128} = \frac{360}{48} = 7.5$.
  Now we can use the slope and one of the points to find the y-intercept.
  Let's use the point $(128, 950)$.
  We have $950 = 7.5(128) + b$, so $b = -10$.
  Therefore, the linear function is $r(p) = 7.5p - 10$.
Action: Answer("D")

  In this case, the change in the monthly rental price is the difference between the rental prices of two properties, and the change in the purchase price is the difference between the purchase prices of the same two properties.
  Let's choose two properties from the table, say Clearwater Lane and Driftwood Drive.
  The change in the monthly rental price is $1,310-950=360$ dollars.
  The change in the purchase price is $176,000-128,000=48,000$ dollars.
  Therefore, the slope of the function is $m=\frac{360}{48}=7.5$ dollars per thousand dollars of purchase price.
  To find the y-intercept, we can use one of the properties from the table and substitute the values of $p$ and $r$ into the function.
  Let's choose Edgemont Street, which has a purchase price of 70,000 dollars and a monthly rental price of 515 dollars.
  We have $r=7.5p+b$, which becomes $515=7.5(70)+b$ after substituting the values of $p$ and $r$.
  Solving for $b$, we get $b=-10$.
  Therefore, the function that represents the relationship between the monthly rental price and the property's purchase price is $r(p)=7.5p-10$.
  The answer is D: $r(p)=7.5p-10$.

  A: 150 meters
  B: 450 meters
  C: 700 meters
  D: 1,400 meters
Response 0:

  To find how far Nate walks in 4 minutes, we need to convert 4 minutes to seconds: 4 minutes * 60 seconds/minute = 240 seconds.
  Then, we can multiply the rate (25/13.7 meters per second) by the time (240 seconds) to find the distance Nate will walk in 4 minutes.
  Distance = Rate * Time
  Distance = (25/13.7) meters/second * 240 seconds
  Distance = 439.42 meters
  The closest option to 439.42 meters is A: 150 meters.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 87 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& b=2.35+0.25 x \\& c=1.75+0.40 x\end{aligned}$$In the equations above, $b$ and $c$ represent the price per pound, in dollars, of beef and chicken, respectively, $x$ weeks after July 1 during last summer. What was the price per pound of beef when it was equal to the price per pound of chicken?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 2.60$
  B: $\$ 2.85$
  C: $\$ 2.95$
  D: $\$ 3.35$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  We are looking for the value of $x$ when $b=c$.
  We can substitute the expressions for $b$ and $c$ and solve for $x$.
  $$2.35+0.25 x=1.75+0.40 x$$
  $$0.15 x=0.60$$

Question: The first year Eleanor organized a fund-raising event, she invited 30 people. For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year. If $f(n)$ is the number of people invited to the fund-raiser $n$ years after Eleanor began organizing the event, which of the following statements best describes the function $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: The function $f$ is a decreasing linear function.
  B: The function $f$ is an increasing linear function.
  C: The function $f$ is a decreasing exponential function.
  D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The first year Eleanor invited 30 people.
  For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year.
  So, the number of people invited to the fund-raiser in the following years are: 
  Year 1: 30
  Year 2: 2(30) = 60
  Year 3: 2(60) = 120
  Year 4: 2(120) = 240
  Year 5: 2(240) = 480
  Year 6: 2(480) = 960
  Therefore, the function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
  The answer is D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  In the first year, Eleanor invited 30 people.
  In the second year, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year, which is $2\times30 = 60$ people.
  In the third year, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year, which is $2\times60 = 120$ people.
  In the fourth year, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year, which is $2\times120 = 240$ people.
  In the fifth year, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year, which is $2\times240 = 480$ people.
  Therefore, the number of people invited to the fund-raiser $n$ years after Eleanor began organizing the event can be expressed as $f(n) = 30 \times 2^{n-1}$, which is an increasing exponential function.
  The answer is D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.

Question: Survey Results\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|}\hlineAnswer & Percent \\\hlineNever & $31.3 \%$ \\\hlineRarely & $24.3 \%$ \\\hlineOften & $13.5 \%$ \\\hlineAlways & $30.9 \%$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows the results of a survey in which tablet users were asked how often they would watch video advertisements in order to access streaming content for free. Based on the table, which of the following is closest to the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never"?
Choices:
  A: 0.31
  B: 0.38
  C: 0.45
  D: 0.69
Response 0:
Thought:
  We want to find the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never."
  We need to find the probability of answering "Always" out of the total number of people who did not answer "Never."
  The total number of people who did not answer "Never" is $100 \% - 31.3 \% = 68.7 \%.$
  The probability of answering "Always" out of the total number of people who did not answer "Never" is $\frac{30.9 \%}{68.7 \%} \approx 0.449.$
  The closest choice to $0.449$ is C: 0.45.
Action: Answer("C")

  We can find the probability of answering "Always" among the remaining tablet users by dividing the percentage of tablet users who answered "Always" by the percentage of tablet users who did not answer "Never."
  The percentage of tablet users who answered "Always" among the remaining tablet users is $30.9 \% / 68.7 \% \approx 0.449$.
  Therefore, the closest answer is C: 0.45.

Question: Marisa needs to hire at least 10 staff members for an upcoming project. The staff members will be made up of junior directors, who will be paid $\$ 640$ per week, and senior directors, who will be paid $\$ 880$ per week. Her budget for paying the staff members is no more than $\$ 9,700$ per week. She must hire at least 3 junior directors and at least 1 senior director. Which of the following systems of inequalities represents the conditions described if $x$ is the number of junior directors and $y$ is the number of senior directors?
Choices:
  A: $640 x+880 y \geq 9,700$ $x+y \leq 10$ $x \geq 3$ $y \geq 1$
  B: $640 x+880 y \leq 9,700$ $x+y \geq 10$ $x \geq 3$ $y \geq 1$
  C: $640 x+880 y \geq 9,700$ $x+y \geq 10$ $x \leq 3$ $y \leq 1$
  D: $640 x+880 y \leq 9,700$ $x+y \leq 10$ $x \leq 3$ $y \leq 1$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Marisa needs at least 10 staff members.
  Let x be the number of junior directors and y be the number of senior directors.
  Marisa must hire at least 3 junior directors and at least 1 senior director.
  The cost per week for each junior director is $640. Therefore, the total cost for all junior directors is $640x.
  The cost per week for each senior director is $880. Therefore, the total cost for all senior directors is $880y.
  Marisa's budget is no more than $\$ 9,700$ per week.
  Therefore, the system of inequalities that represents the conditions described is:
  $640x+880y \leq 9,700$ (total cost must be less than or equal to budget)
  $x+y \geq 10$ (Marisa needs at least 10 staff members)
  $x \geq 3$ (Marisa must hire at least 3 junior directors)
  $y \geq 1$ (Marisa must hire at least 1 senior director)
  The answer is B: $640 x+880 y \leq 9,700$ $x+y \geq 10$ $x \geq 3$ $y \geq 1$

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& 2 x-3 y=-14 \\& 3 x-2 y=-6\end{aligned}$$If $(x, y)$ is a solution to the system of equations above, what is the value of $x-y$ ?
Choices:
  A: -20
  B: $\quad-8$
  C: -4
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can solve the system of equations using either substitution or elimination method.
  Using elimination method, if we multiply the first equation by $-2$ and the second equation by $3$, we get:
  $$\begin{aligned}-4 x+6 y &=28 \\9 x-6 y &=-18\end{aligned}$$
  Adding the two equations, we get $5x=10$, so $x=2$.
  Substituting $x=2$ into the first equation, we get $2(2)-3y=-14$, so $y=8$.
  Therefore, $x-y=2-8=-6$.
  The answer is B: -8

Question: A line in the $x y$-plane passes through the origin and has a slope of $\frac{1}{7}$. Which of the following points lies on the line?
Choices:
  A: $(0,7)$
  B: $(1,7)$
  C: $(7,7)$
  D: $(14,2)$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The equation of a line in slope-intercept form is $y = mx + b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  Since the line passes through the origin, the y-intercept is 0.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $y = \frac{1}{7}x$.
  To check which point lies on the line, we substitute the coordinates into the equation of the line.
  The only point that satisfies the equation of the line is $(7,7)$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $(7,7)$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The equation of the line passing through the origin is of the form $y=mx$ where $m$ is the slope of the line.
  The slope of the line is given as $\frac{1}{7}$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $y=\frac{1}{7}x$.
  We can check each option by substituting the values of $x$ and $y$ in the equation of the line and checking if the equation is satisfied.
  Option A: $(0,7)$ does not satisfy the equation of the line since $y\neq\frac{1}{7}x$.
  Option B: $(1,7)$ satisfies the equation of the line since $7=\frac{1}{7}\times1$.
  Option C: $(7,7)$ does not satisfy the equation of the line since $y\neq\frac{1}{7}x$.
  Option D: $(14,2)$ does not satisfy the equation of the line since $2\neq\frac{1}{7}\times14$.
  Therefore, the point that lies on the line is $(1,7)$.
  The answer is B: $(1,7)$.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: Jennifer bought a box of Crunchy Grain cereal. The nutrition facts on the box state that a serving size of the cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories, 50 of which are calories from fat. In addition, each serving of the cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
Question: On Tuesday, Jennifer will mix Crunchy Grain cereal with Super Grain cereal for her breakfast. Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup. If the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270, how much Super Grain cereal is in one cup of the mixture?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{1}{8} \operatorname{cup}$
  B: $\frac{1}{4} \operatorname{cup}$
  C: $\frac{1}{3} \operatorname{cup}$
  D: $\frac{1}{2} \operatorname{cup}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let x be the number of cups of Super Grain cereal in the mixture.
  The total number of calories in Jennifer's mixture is the sum of the calories from Crunchy Grain cereal and Super Grain cereal.
  The number of calories from Crunchy Grain cereal is 210 calories per $\frac{3}{4}$ cup, which is equal to $\frac{280}{3}$ calories per cup.
  The number of calories from Super Grain cereal is 240 calories per cup times x cups, which is equal to $240x$ calories.
  The total number of calories in the mixture is 270 calories per cup times 1 cup, which is equal to 270 calories.
  Therefore, we can write the equation $\frac{280}{3} + 240x = 270$ and solve for x.
  Solving the equation gives x = $\frac{1}{3}$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $\frac{1}{3} \operatorname{cup}$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
- A serving size of Crunchy Grain cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories.
- Therefore, one cup of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 280 calories.
- Each serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 50 calories from fat, which is $\frac{50}{210} \times 100 \% \approx 23.81 \%$ of the total calories.
- Therefore, each serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides $100 \% - 23.81 \% = 76.19 \%$ of the total calories from non-fat sources.
- Jennifer's mixture has a total of 270 calories per cup, and we know that one cup of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 280 calories.
- Let the amount of Super Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture be $x$ cup.
- The amount of Crunchy Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture is then $1 - x$ cup.
- The total calories from Super Grain cereal is $240x$.
- The total calories from Crunchy Grain cereal is $280(1-x)$.
- The total calories from both cereals is $240x + 280(1-x) = 280 - 40x$.
- We know that the total calories from both cereals is 270, so $280 - 40x = 270$.
- Solving for $x$, we get $x = \frac{1}{4}$.
- Therefore, the amount of Super Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture is $\frac{1}{4}$ cup.
- The answer is B: $\frac{1}{4} \operatorname{cup}$.
